<div id="review_209597457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209597457" />
    <a title="Natalie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3869168-natalie"><img alt="Natalie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326475694p2/3869168.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209597457?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie " href="/user/show/3869168-natalie">Natalie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jenelle, Derick Dupree</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3869168-natalie?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3869168-natalie?shelf=technical-sensual">technical-sensual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3869168-natalie?shelf=the-ocean">the-ocean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3869168-natalie?shelf=travelogue">travelogue</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209597457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4074561598884643671">Book simmering with that Aristotelian flavor: endearing list-making, whimsical archiving. It can be a bit tedious and indulgent at times, like Calvino is spewing out of his vault just to spew, but I have a habit/fault of being an invested and flattering listener, anyway, so I don't mind. In any case, P.'s system of order stresses me out -- it's so intentionally myopic it is smothering. There's no motion to this book at all, but the language is so so beautiful; it was a real pleasure to luxuriate</span>
  <span id="freeText4074561598884643671" style="display:none">Book simmering with that Aristotelian flavor: endearing list-making, whimsical archiving. It can be a bit tedious and indulgent at times, like Calvino is spewing out of his vault just to spew, but I have a habit/fault of being an invested and flattering listener, anyway, so I don't mind. In any case, P.'s system of order stresses me out -- it's so intentionally myopic it is smothering. There's no motion to this book at all, but the language is so so beautiful; it was a real pleasure to luxuriate in it, even if most times I wasn't paying full attention. Just like listening to really interesting people who are all too conscious of their allure. An atmospheric read! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4074561598884643671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5610133-sologdin?shelf=of-best-sentence-and-moost-solaas">of-best-sentence-and-moost-solaas</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3166147187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8002273212285783035">Though he believes that "the world can very well do without him," the res cogitans that inhabits this text (not much of a narrative and accordingly not properly a narrator) investigates the world available to him ("the surface of things is inexhaustible" or so), loathing to waste those surfaces that the world sets before him and attempting to reduce complexity to simplicity, as he asserts.<br/><br/>Plenty of amusing observations and philosophical interest. Perhaps however not entirely successful.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_241871164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241871164" />
    <a title="Brent Legault" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/395634-brent-legault"><img alt="Brent Legault" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194719779p2/395634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241871164?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brent Legault" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brent Legault" href="/user/show/395634-brent-legault">Brent Legault</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241871164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10695982258311160711">If this were a novel (it isn't), it would have the rare distinction of being entirely characterless. (Which is not to say it is without character. Character it has. In fact, it's a real charmer.) <br/><br/>Many books lack plot (as this one does) but few find themselves without a character to follow around. Calvino, however, despite having named his book after a person (the "main character"), has made a world that is populated by things like giraffes and tortoises and waves and meat and cheese and even sta</span>
  <span id="freeText10695982258311160711" style="display:none">If this were a novel (it isn't), it would have the rare distinction of being entirely characterless. (Which is not to say it is without character. Character it has. In fact, it's a real charmer.) <br /><br />Many books lack plot (as this one does) but few find themselves without a character to follow around. Calvino, however, despite having named his book after a person (the "main character"), has made a world that is populated by things like giraffes and tortoises and waves and meat and cheese and even starry skies, but not people. And though Mr. Palomar's wife does make a few brief appearances and some of his friends express their opinions from time to time you, the reader, are meant to know that they are not really there at all or that their presence is unimportant and that it is the thoughts, the observations, the <i>ruminations</i> of Mr. Palomar that are what grant the book its charm, its elegance and its wit.<br /><br />But Mr. Palomar is no more a character in this book than the narrator of a nature documentary. In fact, there were times when I felt that had this been written two or three hundred years ago, it would have been categroized as natural history. Or philosophy. Or confessions.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10695982258311160711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('u0YwXBcM0YR30uwy6xqh7Kehe2Kr2cGIOcaFag5ykeddWCe0b2V/wiD6iDZAttiUnkIK2wAnCWYs5Fx8HKof0Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Era stato lo stesso Pavese a dettare la presentazione del libro. Vi si legge: «Cesare Pavese, che molti si ostinano a considerare un testardo narratore realista, specializzato in campagne e periferie americano-piemontesi, ci scopre in questi Dialoghi un nuovo aspetto del suo temperamento... Nel diario Pavese annotava ancora: «Il mito è un linguaggio, un mezzo espressivo - cioè non qualcosa di arbitrario ma un vivaio di simboli cui appartiene - come a tutti i linguaggi - una particolare sostanza di significati; che null\'altro potrebbe rendere. Con l’espressione “Terzo paesaggio”, Gilles Clément indica tutti i “luoghi abbandonati dall’uomo”: i parchi e le riserve naturali, le grandi aree disabitate del pianeta, ma anche spazi più piccoli e diffusi, quasi invisibili: le aree industriali dismesse dove crescono rovi e sterpaglie; le erbacce al centro di un’aiuola spartitraffico… Sono spazi diversi per forma, dimensione e statuto, accomunati solo dall’assenza di ogni attività umana, ma che presi nel loro insieme sono fondamentali per la conservazione della diversità biologica. Questo piccolo libro ne mostra i meccanismi evolutivi, le connessioni reciproche, l’importanza per il futuro del pianeta. È un’opera di grande densità teorica, che apre un campo di riflessione anche ad implicazioni politiche. “Terzo paesaggio” rinvia a “Terzo stato”, al pamphlet di Seyès del: “Cos’è il Terzo stato? – Tutto. Cosa ha fatto finora? – Niente.           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14938921609982400939">Italo Calvino was born in Cuba and grew up in Italy. He was a journalist and writer of short stories and novels. His best known works include the <i>Our Ancestors</i> trilogy (1952-1959), the <i>Cosmicomics</i> collection of short stories (1965), and the novels <i>Invisible Cities</i> (1972) and <i>If On a Winter's Night a Traveler</i> (1979).<br/><br/>His style is not easy to classify; much of his writing has an air reminiscent to th</span>
  <span id="freeText14938921609982400939" style="display:none">Italo Calvino was born in Cuba and grew up in Italy. He was a journalist and writer of short stories and novels. His best known works include the <i>Our Ancestors</i> trilogy (1952-1959), the <i>Cosmicomics</i> collection of short stories (1965), and the novels <i>Invisible Cities</i> (1972) and <i>If On a Winter's Night a Traveler</i> (1979).<br /><br />His style is not easy to classify; much of his writing has an air reminiscent to that of fantastical fairy tales (<i>Our Ancestors, Cosmicomics</i>), although sometimes his writing is more "realistic" and in the scenic mode of observation (<i>Difficult Loves</i>, for example). Some of his writing has been called <i>postmodern</i>, reflecting on literature and the act of reading, while some has been labeled magical realist, others fables, others simply "modern". He wrote: "<i>My working method has more often than not involved the subtraction of weight. I have tried to remove weight, sometimes from people, sometimes from heavenly bodies, sometimes from cities; above all I have tried to remove weight from the structure of stories and from language.</i>"<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14938921609982400939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2678548-palomar">Quotes from Mr Palomar</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;A person's life consists of a collection of events, <br />the last of which could also change the meaning of the whole, <br />not because it counts more than the previous ones<br />but because once they are included in a life, <br />events are arranged in an order that is not chronological but, rather, <br />corresponds to an inner architecture.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/433634-a-person-s-life-consists-of-a-collection-of-events-the">44 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;A person, for example, reads in adulthood a book that is important for him, and it makes him say, "How could I have lived without reading it!" and also, "What a pity I did not read it in my youth!" Well, these statements do not have much meaning, especially the second, because after he has read that book, his life becomes the life of a person who has read that book, and it is of little importance whether he read it early or late, because now his life before that reading also assumes a form shaped by that reading.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7496988-a-person-for-example-reads-in-adulthood-a-book-that">10 likes</a>
            </nobr>
